<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:DMX_Signature.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/DMX_Signature.png/150px-DMX_Signature.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="86" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/DMX_Signature.png/225px-DMX_Signature.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/DMX_Signature.png/300px-DMX_Signature.png 2x" data-file-width="463" data-file-height="265" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Earl Simmons</b> (December 18, 1970 – April 9, 2021), known professionally as <b>DMX</b>, was an American rapper and actor. He is regarded as one of the most important figures of 2000s <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:bey_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:bey-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> His music is characterized by his "aggressive" rapping style,<sup id="cite_ref-:hard_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:hard-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> with his lyrical content varying from <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip_hop" title="Hardcore hip hop">hardcore</a> themes to <a href="/wiki/Prayer" title="Prayer">prayers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began rapping in the early 1990s and released his debut album <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Dark_and_Hell_Is_Hot" title="It&#39;s Dark and Hell Is Hot">It's Dark and Hell Is Hot</a></i> in 1998, to both critical acclaim and commercial success, selling 251,000 copies within its first week of release.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> DMX released his best-selling album, <i><a href="/wiki/..._And_Then_There_Was_X" title="... And Then There Was X">... And Then There Was X</a></i>, in 1999, which included the hit single "<a href="/wiki/Party_Up_(Up_in_Here)" title="Party Up (Up in Here)">Party Up (Up in Here)</a>". His 2003 singles "<a href="/wiki/Where_the_Hood_At%3F" title="Where the Hood At?">Where the Hood At?</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/X_Gon%27_Give_It_to_Ya" title="X Gon&#39; Give It to Ya">X Gon' Give It to Ya</a>" were also commercially successful. He was the first artist to debut an album at No.1 five times in a row on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> charts.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> DMX sold over 74 million records worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX was featured in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Belly_(film)" title="Belly (film)">Belly</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Romeo_Must_Die" title="Romeo Must Die">Romeo Must Die</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Exit_Wounds" title="Exit Wounds">Exit Wounds</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cradle_2_the_Grave" title="Cradle 2 the Grave">Cradle 2 the Grave</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Hour" title="Last Hour">Last Hour</a></i>. In 2006, he starred in the reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/DMX:_Soul_of_a_Man" title="DMX: Soul of a Man">DMX: Soul of a Man</a></i>, which was primarily aired on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable television</a> network. In 2003, he published a book of his memoirs titled <i>E.A.R.L.: The Autobiography of DMX</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Earl Simmons was born on December 18, 1970, in Mount Vernon, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He was the son of 19-year-old Arnett Simmons and 18-year-old Joe Barker.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Earl was Simmons' second child; she had given birth to a daughter, Bonita, two years prior, and later gave birth to one daughter, Shayla, and two stillborn sons.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> His father, Barker, was an artist who painted <a href="/wiki/Watercolor_painting" title="Watercolor painting">watercolor paintings</a> of street scenes to sell at local fairs. Barker moved to Philadelphia and was largely absent from his life.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a child, Simmons suffered greatly from bronchial asthma, being taken to the emergency room almost nightly due to him waking up unable to breathe.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He was raised as a <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witness" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witness">Jehovah's Witness</a> but became disillusioned with the faith after an incident where he was hit by a drunk driver while crossing the street. A month later, an insurance representative went to his house to try and reach an agreement to prevent his family from suing. Simmons claims he was told that his family could have been awarded a settlement of $10,000 and possibly even more for the injuries he sustained. However, his mother rejected the settlement as she claimed that Jehovah's Witnesses are taught to be self-sufficient, although the group's official doctrine at the time did not prohibit suing or receiving settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Simmons went through a disjointed childhood that included being beaten by his mother and her various boyfriends so badly that he lost teeth and sustained numerous bruises and cuts on his face. When Simmons was five years old, his family settled into the School Street Projects in
Yonkers, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> When he was six years old, his mother knocked out two of his teeth with a broom after he erased something in her notebook.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> At school, he threw chairs at teachers and stabbed another child in the face with a pencil.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> When he was seven, an aunt got him drunk on vodka. The same year, he was jailed for stealing cakes from a market.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> One summer, his mother locked him in his bedroom, allowing him to only exit for trips to the bathroom.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the fifth grade, at age 10, Simmons was expelled from school and sent to the Julia Dyckman Andrus Children's Home for 18 months. X states that he actually enjoyed it there at first. He got 3 good meals with a dessert every day, an allowance every week, colored TV's and stereo's he could use, and occasional vacations. Also for Christmas the school gave each child $25. Every so often, Earl would receive visits from his family which he described as his favorite times. They would go out on the lawn and play frisbee, sleigh ride when it was snowy and just socialise.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Earl and a kid he met at the group home decided to experiment like kids do. They wanted to see if they lit a blue flame to the basement floor, would the floor turn blue. he was charged with arson, after this he and the kid (Adam) started fighting a lot and it became a major problem. X attempted to choke him to death one day and was taken from the normal school population and had to stay in an unused office during school hours. He also had to move out of his cottage and live in the infirmary.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Constantly away from other children, from going and playing outside, and enjoying all the other privileges. Later, Earl was sent to Children's Village. In what he described as a defining moment of betrayal, his mother tricked him by telling him they were just visiting the home, then she enrolled him there.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When he was 14, Earl returned to Yonkers. Simmons began living between the streets, his grandmas and couch surfing at a friend's house. This had been regular for X since he was a young child, even sleeping in <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> clothing bins a few times. At a young age he began to feel a connection to dogs, and started befriending stray dogs and even stealing dogs.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-song_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-song-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
During his time in group homes he had started beatboxing and became very engaged with Hip Hop.
After performing for his friends, they encouraged Simmons to continue writing music at the behest of his teacher. When he returned home, Simmons met Ready Ron, a local rapper, who was impressed with Simmons' beatboxing skills and asked him to become his partner. Simmons chose the name "DMX", which came from an instrument he had used at the boys' home, the <a href="/wiki/Oberheim_DMX" title="Oberheim DMX">Oberheim DMX</a> <a href="/wiki/Drum_machine" title="Drum machine">drum machine</a>. It later was also interpreted as "Divine Master Of The Unknown" and "Dark Man X".<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-song_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-song-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a freshman at <a href="/wiki/Yonkers_Middle_High_School" title="Yonkers Middle High School">Yonkers Middle High School</a>, DMX was the second-fastest on the track-and-field varsity team. However, he had bad grades and a sparse attendance record.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He turned to robbery as a way of making money to eat and buy clothes, jewellery and stuff for his dog: his first was a purse <a href="/wiki/Snatch_theft" title="Snatch theft">snatch theft</a> in Yonkers that netted him $1,000 (equivalent to $2,800&#32;in 2022), which he used to buy a leather dog collar and dog harness for his dog, and a pair of <a href="/wiki/The_Timberland_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="The Timberland Company">Timberland</a> boots for himself.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> After celebrating a friends birthday, X hit a blunt handed to him by Ready Ron. It was laced with crack, shortly after Earl had build up a strong addiction to crack. By the end of the year, he attended school just to rob people and was robbing three people per day to fund his addiction for crack.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He also started <a href="/wiki/Carjacking" title="Carjacking">carjacking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-agony_17-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agony-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> X was locked up for a few months for stealing a dog. Later after being released went to school with a shotgun strapped to his leg one day to commit a robbery, and a few days later was arrested again and sentenced to 2 years at Industry Institution in upstate New York.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The juvenile prison was a low security unit slightly south of Rochester, and if you were heading anywhere but north was completely in the middle of nowhere. 2 days in Earl and his cellmate, a white kid from an upstate town escaped. They walked 3 days in the snow to the town Earl's cellmate lived in. They stayed in the basement of a friends house, and there his accomplice left Earl by himself. Earl was found by the family and they fed him and let him stay until they gave him money to get home for his birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1988 while Earl was in the Hamptons with a friend that he drove in a stolen car, he was arrested and his "friend" snitched on him giving police all the information they needed. He was sent to Suffolk County Jail where he battled other inmates, namely <a href="/wiki/K-Solo" title="K-Solo">K-Solo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Musical career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1985.E2.80.931995:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1985–1995:_Career_beginnings">1985–1995: Career beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1985–1995: Career beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX got his start in performing at age 14, in 1985, when he beatboxed for Ready Ron. They would do small shows together where Ready Ron would control the mic as the Emcee, and DMX would beatbox and adlib for Ron. After a while he came to a realization that the Rapper was always the person getting all of the attention, so he decided to start rapping himself. Going by the name "DMX", meaning "Divine Master Of The Unknown" and later "Darkman X".<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> After serving a 2-year prison sentence, he began writing his own lyrics and performing at the local recreation center for younger children. In 1988, while in prison for carjacking, he began dedicating almost all of his free time to writing lyrics and battling other inmates.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> During this time he had created a style called "Spellbound" where he spelled each word out letter by letter. While in Suffolk County Jail he met up and coming rapper <a href="/wiki/K-Solo" title="K-Solo">K-Solo</a> and they engaged in a battle.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> X claims to have used the spellbound style to defeat him, and <a href="/wiki/K-Solo" title="K-Solo">K-Solo</a> claims to have created and used the spellbound style to win against DMX. After the battle they gained respect for each over and became friends. DMX was released in 1988, but spent majority of 1989 locked up as well. Upon being released in late 1989, he began producing and selling his own mixtapes where he rapped over instrumentals from other songs and sold them on street corners, which helped him build a local fan base all over Yonkers. At the time he was working with a Yonkers DJ called DJ Kasun.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1990 shortly after DMX's release from prison, <a href="/wiki/K-Solo" title="K-Solo">K-Solo</a> released his single "Spellbound". From here DMX felt as if K-Solo had stolen his style and began making tracks dissing him and putting them on mixtapes.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 1990 his DJ, Kasun was locked up and another local DJ named Superior became DMX's main DJ and close friend.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> X began going all around New York performing at shows, battling over rappers and selling his mixtapes. In November 1990 DMX battled Bill Blass at School 12, Yonkers. This makes the audio on YouTube potentially the oldest recording of DMX. They eventually rematched the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Around this time X was being managed by Jack McNasty, and had created a demo tape produced by House Party Productions.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The demo tape consisted of the tracks "Spellbound", "Critical Condition", "Unstoppable Force", "Three Little Pigs" and "The Original Author Of Spellbound" (a diss track dedicated to K-Solo). He made his first radio appearance in December 1990 on WBLS, where he was interviewed and spit his Spellbound style live a cappella.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Currently going by "DMX The Great", he made an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stretch_Armstrong_and_Bobbito_Show" title="The Stretch Armstrong and Bobbito Show">The Stretch Armstrong and Bobbito Show</a></i> in January 1991 with Percee P, where they both freestyled.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the same month, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a></i> magazine praised DMX in its <i>Unsigned Hype</i> column that highlighted unsigned hip-hop artists.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> DMX continued to put out mixtapes, and in 1992 under "Ruff Ryders Ent." he put out his first single "Born Loser/Catching The Same Hell" independently. Later this year <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> signed DMX to its subsidiary label <a href="/wiki/Ruffhouse_Records" title="Ruffhouse Records">Ruffhouse Records</a>, which released his major debut single "Born Loser" in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoodmx_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoodmx-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After the single didn't achieve as much success as expected due to poor promotion, X finished his contract with Ruffhouse and was now an independent artist.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 1994 <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a> had approached Ruff Ryders to sign DMX. They came to Powerhouse Studios in Yonkers after <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a> had finished a show in New York. X spit for them and they were impressed with what they heard, the next week they flew Ruff Ryders out to Los Angeles to finalise signing DMX. Eventually they decided not to sign to Death Row since they couldn't reach the right agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> During 1993 and 1994 X was staying in Baltimore with Waah Dean, Darin "Dee" Dean and the rest of the original Ruff Ryders. One night X took a cab all the way from Baltimore to The Bronx to battle Jay Z. Both sides claim to have won, with the final result being decided as a draw.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Later this year he independently released his single, "Make a Move" with "Cant Touch Me Kid" as the B-Side. He also recorded another single "Up To No Good", produced by SpunkBigga. A music video was even shot for the song, filmed in Mulford Gardens, Yonkers where DMX lived, and 125th in Harlem, Manhattan. For unknown reasons the song was never released. He made his first guest appearance alongside <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mic_Geronimo" title="Mic Geronimo">Mic Geronimo</a> on the classic underground track "Time to Build" on Mic Geronimo's debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In late 1994 DMX was sentenced to around a year of prison time for criminal possession of a weapon, and did his time in Valhalla Correctional Facility.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He was released around late 1995, and began featuring on songs with Pudgee Tha Phat Bastard, Cash Money Click, Black Child and <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.931997:_Building_hype.2C_coming_close_to_death_and_signing_to_Def_Jam"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–1997:_Building_hype,_coming_close_to_death_and_signing_to_Def_Jam">1996–1997: Building hype, coming close to death and signing to Def Jam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1996–1997: Building hype, coming close to death and signing to Def Jam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During 1995 and 1996 DMX would spend a lot of time putting together mixtapes with DJs such as Superior, Crazy Rob and Steve Black. Around this time fellow Ruff Ryder's <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">The Lox</a> were signed to <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a>, and had Harlem producer <a href="/wiki/Dame_Grease" title="Dame Grease">Dame Grease</a> create a large percentage of their beats. Eventually after a while of trying to convince him, Waah Dean signed <a href="/wiki/Dame_Grease" title="Dame Grease">Dame Grease</a> as a producer for Ruff Ryders. Waah and Darin "Dee" Dean approached <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a> in the interest of getting DMX a deal, but Puffy claimed that DMX was not marketable enough.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> DMX started making tracks with production by <a href="/wiki/Dame_Grease" title="Dame Grease">Dame Grease</a> and PK, including a classic unreleased single called "Deeper".<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Around this time DMX started to feel very pessimistic, and was under the impression that he would never succeed in the rap game.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> However, in the summer of 1996 one of the songs DMX, <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">The Lox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a> had recorded, "Niggaz Done Started Something" became a mixtape/street hit. It was featured on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue" title="DJ Clue">DJ Clue</a>'s "Summatyme Shootout Pt.1 (1996)" mixtape, DJ S&amp;S's "Bad Boy Vol. IV, Stop Yappin' (1996)" mixtape to name a couple. This song alone gave DMX a huge buzz, and later in November 1996 DMX made his first major mixtape exclusive appearance with the "Ghetto Life" freestyle on Ron G's "Street Dreams (1996)" mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX was really starting to build up some hype in the streets, however one night in December 1996 X was brutally jumped and almost died. Earlier that evening he had picked up a chain he saw someone drop during a police chase, and was wearing a <a href="/wiki/Avirex" title="Avirex">Avirex</a> jacket he had stolen from someone's back yard weeks earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> While hanging out around "Slow bomb" projects, DMX was told people were looking for him believing that he had robbed a 16 year old for both the jacket and chain. DMX did not rob the kid, however the chain he took was robbed from the kid before X took it himself. He agreed to meet them, and explain to them he did not commit the robbery and was willing to hand over the possessions.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> DMX met the father, uncles and multiple other people with the child who were looking for him in an alley way and handed them the jacket and chain, DMX tried to explain the situation but the kid persisted that DMX was indeed the person who robbed him. Suddenly, X was grabbed and the father began to punch him to the ground with the whole group brutally punching and stomping him out without any restraint.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> after a while of the group stomping him out they began to drag him into a nearby park on Locust Hill, with other people on the street even joining in after hearing the false news that DMX had robbed a child. After minutes more of beating him the group began to leave him lying almost lifeless in the park, when one of the men started walking back with a brick to launch it at DMX's head.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Earl's survival instinct kicked in and he mustered all the strength in his body and managed to stumble away with the brick missing him. DMX described this as revenge for everyone he had ever robbed, and a lesson given to him by god.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> An ambulance found him lying in a pile of blood a block away from the scene of the beating, he was taken to Yonkers General Hospital where he was sent home with the doctors claiming he hadn't broke anything and that he would be fine. 2 days later his throat had swelled up so much that he could barely breathe so Tashera Simmons took him to Valhalla Correctional Facility's hospital, where DMX's uncle was a Correctional Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The doctors claimed that if he did not come to the hospital that day, that he would have died. They did an X-Ray on him and found that he had broken his jaw in multiple places and had many serious injuries. For 4 months DMX had his jaw wired, and had to eat only liquid food through a straw.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly before this event DMX's associate <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Irv Gotti</a> became an A&amp;R for <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>, and was telling DMX that <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> co-president <a href="/wiki/Lyor_Cohen" title="Lyor Cohen">Lyor Cohen</a> was willing to come to Powerhouse Studios in Yonkers to hear DMX and other local rappers in Yonkers.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> DMX claimed he didn't care when even if his jaw was indeed wired and he couldn't even speak properly, so the next night Lyor came to Powerhouse. DMX spit his best material and performed for almost an hour, with the maximum intensity, passion and emotion even with his jaw being wired shut. Lyor jumped up in the air amazed by DMX's performance and decided to sign DMX to <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998-2000:_Debut_album_and_commercial_success">1998-2000: Debut album and commercial success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1998-2000: Debut album and commercial success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March–April 1997, DMX had the wires taken out of his mouth. The same day he and <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">The Lox</a> recorded the famous "Get At Me Dog Freestyle" for <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue" title="DJ Clue">DJ Clue</a>'s "Clueminatti: The New World Order" mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The beat and verse 3 from his unreleased single "Deeper" were used to later make his debut Def Jam single "Get At Me Dog". DMX recorded tracks from April 1997 to January 1998 for his debut album. During this time, his guest appearances on <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a>'s singles "<a href="/wiki/24_Hrs._to_Live" title="24 Hrs. to Live">24 Hrs. to Live</a>" and "Take What's Yours", <a href="/wiki/D-Block_(hip_hop)" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Block (hip hop)">The LOX</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Money,_Power_%26_Respect_(song)" title="Money, Power &amp; Respect (song)">Money, Power &amp; Respect</a>", and <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/4,_3,_2,_1_(LL_Cool_J_song)" title="4, 3, 2, 1 (LL Cool J song)">4, 3, 2, 1</a>" created a strong buzz for his up-and-coming album.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In February 1998, he released his debut major-label single "<a href="/wiki/Get_at_Me_Dog" title="Get at Me Dog">Get at Me Dog</a>" on <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>. The single received an <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">RIAA certification</a> of gold.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> His first major-label album <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Dark_and_Hell_Is_Hot" title="It&#39;s Dark and Hell Is Hot">It's Dark and Hell Is Hot</a></i>, which included the single "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>", was then released in May 1998. The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart in the U.S. and sold over five million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In December 1998, he released his album <i><a href="/wiki/Flesh_of_My_Flesh,_Blood_of_My_Blood" title="Flesh of My Flesh, Blood of My Blood">Flesh of My Flesh, Blood of My Blood</a></i>. It debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 and went multi-platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoodmx_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoodmx-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He released his third and best-selling album <i><a href="/wiki/..._And_Then_There_Was_X" title="... And Then There Was X">... And Then There Was X</a></i>, on December 21, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It was his third album to debut at number one on the Billboard 200. Its most popular single, "<a href="/wiki/Party_Up_(Up_in_Here)" title="Party Up (Up in Here)">Party Up (Up in Here)</a>", became his first <a href="/wiki/Record_chart" title="Record chart">Top Ten</a> hit on the <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> charts, and was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2001_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Grammy Awards">2001 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-grammyawards_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammyawards-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The album was certified six-times Platinum, and was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Album" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2001_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Grammy Awards">2001 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-grammyawards_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammyawards-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, DMX also made a cameo appearance in the <a href="/wiki/Sum_41" title="Sum 41">Sum 41</a> music video for "<a href="/wiki/Makes_No_Difference" title="Makes No Difference">Makes No Difference</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2001.E2.80.932004:_Return_to_music"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001–2004:_Return_to_music">2001–2004: Return to music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2001–2004: Return to music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After improving his legal situation, DMX returned to the studio to complete his fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Depression_(DMX_album)" title="The Great Depression (DMX album)">The Great Depression</a></i>. With its release on October 23, 2001, it was his fourth album to debut at number one on the Billboard 200, featuring the singles "Who We Be", "We Right Here", and "Shorty Was The Bomb". Despite the album's triple Platinum certification, its commercial and critical success was lower than his previous album.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> His fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Champ" title="Grand Champ">Grand Champ</a></i>, released in September 2003, once again debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 and included the singles "Where the Hood At?" and "Get It on the Floor". After its release, he informed the public that he planned to retire and that <i>Grand Champ</i> was his final album.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932011:_Year_of_the_Dog...Again_and_The_Definition_of_X"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2011:_Year_of_the_Dog...Again_and_The_Definition_of_X">2005–2011: <i>Year of the Dog...Again</i> and <i>The Definition of X</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2005–2011: Year of the Dog...Again and The Definition of X">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg/170px-Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg/255px-Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg/340px-Academy_Awards_afterparty_CUN_DMX.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1172" data-file-height="1756" /></a><figcaption>DMX in February 2007</figcaption></figure>
<p>DMX signed to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> in January 2006. He recorded his next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Year_of_the_Dog..._Again" title="Year of the Dog... Again">Year of the Dog... Again</a></i>, while switching record labels, which caused numerous delays.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> It was released on August 1, 2006, and missed the number one Billboard spot by only a few hundred copies.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He released two more singles, "<a href="/wiki/Lord_Give_Me_a_Sign" title="Lord Give Me a Sign">Lord Give Me a Sign</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/We_in_Here" title="We in Here">We in Here</a>". On June 12, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> released a compilation of his greatest hits <i><a href="/wiki/The_Definition_of_X:_The_Pick_of_the_Litter" title="The Definition of X: The Pick of the Litter">The Definition of X: The Pick of the Litter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Def Jam released another compilation album, <i>The Best of DMX</i>, which features hit singles including "<a href="/wiki/Where_the_Hood_At%3F" title="Where the Hood At?">Where the Hood At?</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/X_Gon%27_Give_It_to_Ya" title="X Gon&#39; Give It to Ya">X Gon' Give It to Ya</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, DMX claimed he would pursue preaching in Jersey City, New Jersey as well as continue to produce music. He completed a <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">Gospel music</a> album prior to his incarceration. According to MTV, he had semi-retired to study the Bible in an effort to give messages behind the pulpit.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932013:_Undisputed"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2013:_Undisputed">2011–2013: <i>Undisputed</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2011–2013: Undisputed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 11, 2011, DMX performed at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>. He stated that he has been working "nonstop, every day" on his seventh album, which was titled <i><a href="/wiki/Undisputed_(DMX_album)" title="Undisputed (DMX album)">Undisputed</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A video for a new track titled "Last Hope" was released via the Internet on September 24, 2011, and was later included on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Weigh_In" class="mw-redirect" title="The Weigh In">The Weigh In</a></i> EP released digitally on May 5, 2012. In late February 2012, <a href="/wiki/Seven_Arts_Pictures" title="Seven Arts Pictures">Seven Arts Pictures</a> acquired the catalog of DMX's music and signed DMX to a two-album deal.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> During a performance at New York's <a href="/wiki/Santos_Party_House" title="Santos Party House">Santos Party House</a> on December 25, 2011, DMX stated that the new album would be titled <i>Undisputed</i> and would be released on March 26, 2012. After numerous delays,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> the album was eventually released on September 11, 2012, and featured production from <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a> and <a href="/wiki/J.R._Rotem" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R. Rotem">J.R. Rotem</a> with a guest appearance by <a href="/wiki/Machine_Gun_Kelly_(musician)" title="Machine Gun Kelly (musician)">MGK</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932021:_Def_Jam_reunion_and_Exodus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2021:_Def_Jam_reunion_and_Exodus">2013–2021: Def Jam reunion and <i>Exodus</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2013–2021: Def Jam reunion and Exodus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, DMX announced he had begun working on his eighth studio album. He collaborated with producers Swizz Beatz<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dame_Grease" title="Dame Grease">Dame Grease</a>. In December, after regaining his passport, he embarked on a world tour with performances in Bulgaria and Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On January 7, 2015, Seven Arts Music announced that DMX would be releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Redemption_of_the_Beast" title="Redemption of the Beast">Redemption of the Beast</a></i> the following week; however, close personal friend and recurring collaborator producer/rapper/entrepreneur Swizz Beatz and DMX's management confirmed that this was false.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On January 13, 2015, Seven Arts Music released <i>Redemption of the Beast</i>, without acquiring a legal artist contract. On January 15, 2015, it was announced by DMX's brother/manager Montana that DMX was no longer signed to Seven Arts Music and that they would be taking legal action against Seven Arts Music for the unauthorized release of <i>Redemption of the Beast</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Long-time collaborator Swizz Beatz stated that two of the collaborators on the album would be <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> His 2003 song "X Gon' Give It to Ya" was featured in the 2016 film <i><a href="/wiki/Deadpool_(film)" title="Deadpool (film)">Deadpool</a></i> and in its trailers. On June 28, 2016, DMX released a new song titled "Blood Red" and produced by Divine Bars.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On January 11, 2017, DMX released a new song produced by Swizz Beats titled "Bain Iz Back".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On September 20, 2019, DMX signed a new record deal with <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>, reuniting with the label for the first time since his 2003 album <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Champ" title="Grand Champ">Grand Champ</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX's eighth and first posthumous studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Exodus_(DMX_album)" title="Exodus (DMX album)">Exodus</a></i> was released through Def Jam on May 28, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
DMX was a born-again Christian,<sup id="cite_ref-readsbible_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readsbible-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and stated that he read the Bible every day.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-calling_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calling-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> While in jail, DMX stated that he had a purpose for being there: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"I came here to meet somebody...Don't know who it was, but I'll know when I see him. And I came here to give him a message. And that message is Jesus loves them."<sup id="cite_ref-calling_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calling-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p> DMX was a <a href="/wiki/Transitional_deacon" class="mw-redirect" title="Transitional deacon">transitional deacon</a> and aspired to become ordained as a pastor, stating that he received this <a href="/wiki/Religious_calling" title="Religious calling">call</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, he gave a sermon at a church in Phoenix, Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships_and_children">Relationships and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Relationships and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX was the father of 17 children from 11 different women.<sup id="cite_ref-curse_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curse-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VladTVDMX_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VladTVDMX-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He married his childhood friend Tashera Simmons in 1999 and they were married for 11 years.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcobituary_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcobituary-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> They had four children together: Xavier (born 1992), Tacoma (born 1999), Sean (born 2002), and Praise Mary Ella (born 2005).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In July 2010, after his first of three incarcerations that year, Tashera announced their separation.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> They remained friends,<sup id="cite_ref-bbcobituary_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcobituary-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> although in 2016, Tashera accused DMX of missing his $10,000/month <a href="/wiki/Child_support" title="Child support">child support</a> payment.<sup id="cite_ref-baby_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baby-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX had a daughter, Sasha (born 2002), with Patricia Trejo.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Trejo sued DMX for $1&#160;million in unpaid child support. The case was settled in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX and Monique Wayne, a Maryland resident, fought over her claim that he was the father of her son born in 2004. She sued him for defamation and for child support.<sup id="cite_ref-vacates_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vacates-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> After genetic testing proved that DMX was the father, in January 2008, DMX was ordered to pay Wayne $1.5&#160;million, but a judge vacated the judgment in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-vacates_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vacates-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX also fathered a child and two daughters in 2008 with Yadira Borrego.<sup id="cite_ref-kids_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kids-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX's fifteenth child was born to his fiancée Desiree Lindstrom on August 16, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-kids_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kids-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baby_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baby-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 5, 2019, DMX's sixteenth and seventeenth children, twin boys, were born to Pebbles Junell.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX did not have a will.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> As a result, legal battles ensued in probate courts following his death.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances_and_bankruptcies">Finances and bankruptcies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Finances and bankruptcies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX filed for bankruptcy three times.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> His first filing was on July 30, 2013, citing his child support obligations as his priority claim.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The filing was challenged by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Trustee_Program" title="United States Trustee Program">United States Trustee Program</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and was dismissed by the U.S. Bankruptcy Court in Manhattan on November 11, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feud_with_Ja_Rule">Feud with Ja Rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Feud with Ja Rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1990s, DMX formed a close bond with fellow up-and-coming rappers <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a>. The three collaborated many times and formed a group known as <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._(rap_group)" title="Murder Inc. (rap group)">Murder Inc.</a> The group was short-lived due to internal issues between DMX and Jay-Z. After the breakup of Murder Inc., DMX disparaged Ja Rule in interviews, accusing him of being a copycat, drawing comparisons between himself and what he saw as Ja stealing his signature "gruff" style of delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-diss_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diss-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX released the <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss track</a> "They Want War" on a 2002 <a href="/wiki/DJ_Kay_Slay" title="DJ Kay Slay">DJ Kay Slay</a> mixtape; Ja Rule never directly responded.<sup id="cite_ref-diss_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diss-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a> also released the single "Go to Sleep" with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obie_Trice" title="Obie Trice">Obie Trice</a> as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Cradle_2_the_Grave" title="Cradle 2 the Grave">Cradle 2 the Grave</a></i> soundtrack with numerous lines directed to <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a>. However, as time passed and the feud faded into obscurity, DMX said that he wanted to officially bring it to an end when he was released from prison in 2005: "<a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Gotti</a> came to me in jail and said I want to make peace with you and him. I was like, 'Alright Gotti, let's do it."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, DMX and Ja Rule did not officially end their feud until 2009, at VH1's <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Honors" title="Hip Hop Honors">Hip Hop Honors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feud_with_Jay-Z">Feud with Jay-Z</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Feud with Jay-Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When DMX partnered with <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a> in Murder Inc., there was a feud between the two, which also contributed to the failure of the group and working together. According to reports, the feud started in the early 1990s after a rap battle between the two, which led to DMX's disdain for Jay-Z.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_2015-11-10_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_2015-11-10-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meaww_2021-04-08_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meaww_2021-04-08-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Prior to DMX's death, the feud, although it fizzled out over the years, continued on when DMX said in an Instagram video that he wanted to rap battle Jay-Z on <a href="/wiki/Verzuz" title="Verzuz">Verzuz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Urban_Islandz_2020-05-21_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Urban_Islandz_2020-05-21-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DMX_mug_shot.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/DMX_mug_shot.jpg/220px-DMX_mug_shot.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/DMX_mug_shot.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="375" /></a><figcaption>DMX's June 2008 mugshot</figcaption></figure>
<p>DMX was in jail 30+ times<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> for various offenses, including criminal possession of a weapon, robbery, assault, carjacking, animal cruelty, reckless driving, driving under the influence, unlicensed driving, drug possession, probation violation, failure to pay child support, pretending to be a federal agent, and tax evasion.
</p>
<h3><span id="1986.E2.80.931988"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1986–1988">1986–1988</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1986–1988">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX was first sent to prison in 1986 after stealing a dog from a junkyard. He served a few months in the juvenile unit of Woodfield Prison in Valhalla, New York. Later this year he was sentenced to 2 years for another crime and sent to Industry Institution (Now named OCFS-Industry Residential Center) in upstate New York.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> However, in December 1986, just a few days after starting his sentence, he and his cellmate successfully escaped the prison and DMX returned home until his mother forced him to turn himself in and finish his sentence, which he did at the McCormick Juvenile Detention Centre in Brooktondale, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Simmons was sent to prison again in 1988 for <a href="/wiki/Carjacking" title="Carjacking">carjacking</a>, and was later moved to a higher security prison after attempting to extort a fellow inmate for drugs. He was released in the summer of 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989">1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX was charged with fourth degree grand larceny (155.30) in January 1989 and served a 9-month sentence. (As shown in police report shown in BET's Ruff Ryders Chronicles documentary. No reference available to cite)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1992">1992</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1992">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX was charged with criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree (220.03), no disposition reported
(As shown in police report shown in BET's Ruff Ryders Chronicles documentary. No reference available to cite)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1993">1993</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1993">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During his time in Baltimore DMX <sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> was charged for multiple crimes. The first being in March, with him being charged with criminal sale in the third degree of a controlled substance (220.39), no disposition reported. The second being criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree (220.03), no disposition reported.
(As shown in police report shown in BET's Ruff Ryders Chronicles documentary. No reference available to cite)
It's possible DMX also served time in late 1993 since he claim he is "fresh off a bid" in his 1994 track "Can't Touch Me Kid". This is just theory since there is no evidence to support this claim.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1994-1995">1994-1995</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 1994-1995">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late 1994 DMX was sentenced and charged with criminal possession of weapon and served around a year (the exact time served/sentenced is unknown) in Valhalla Correctional Facility. (As shown in police report shown in BET's Ruff Ryders Chronicles documentary. No reference available to cite) <sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> (as shown in December 1994 prison letter from DMX in DJ Superiors "The Man Who Walked The Dog" book, No reference available to cite). On his third day there, he spat in the face of a captain and was sentenced to 1 year and 1 month of solitary confinement. He was put in Lockdown Block 3K <sup id="cite_ref-earl_5-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earl-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and sometime in late 1995 finished his sentence.
</p>
<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.931999"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998–1999">1998–1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1998–1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>When officers of the Fort Lee Police Department executed a search of his home in 1999, DMX promptly surrendered himself on weapons possession charges.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>DMX faced a 1999 animal cruelty charge in Teaneck, New Jersey after a dozen pit bulls were found at his home there;<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> the charge was dismissed after the performer agreed to accept responsibility and record public service announcements for an animal rights group.<sup id="cite_ref-held_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-held-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932005_Metro_NY"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000–2005_Metro_NY">2000–2005 Metro NY</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2000–2005 Metro NY">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>In 2000, DMX served a 15-day jail sentence for possession of marijuana.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>DMX served another jail sentence in 2001 for driving without a license and possession of marijuana. His appeal to reduce the sentence was denied; rather, he was charged with assault for throwing objects at prison guards.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In January 2002, DMX pleaded guilty in New Jersey to 13 counts of animal cruelty, two counts of maintaining a nuisance, and one count each of disorderly conduct and possession of drug paraphernalia. He eventually plea-bargained down to fines, probation, and community service and starred in public service announcements against the dangers of guns and animal abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In June 2004, DMX was arrested at the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a>, on charges of cocaine possession, criminal impersonation, criminal possession of a weapon, criminal mischief, menacing, and driving under the influence of drugs or alcohol, while claiming to be a federal agent and attempting to <a href="/wiki/Carjack" class="mw-redirect" title="Carjack">carjack</a> a vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He was given a conditional discharge on December 8, 2004, but pleaded guilty on October 25, 2005, to violating <a href="/wiki/Parole" title="Parole">parole</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On November 18, 2005, DMX was sentenced to 70 days in jail at <a href="/wiki/Riker%27s_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Riker&#39;s Island">Riker's Island</a> for violating parole; the lateness charge added a 10-day extension to the original 60-day sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> DMX was released early (for "<a href="/wiki/Good_conduct_time" title="Good conduct time">good behavior</a>") on December 30, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>In 2007, DMX's home was raided on reports of animal cruelty.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.932011_Arizona_and_California"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–2011_Arizona_and_California">2008–2011 Arizona and California</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2008–2011 Arizona and California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>On May 9, 2008, DMX was arrested on drug and animal cruelty charges after attempting to barricade himself inside his home in Cave Creek, Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-held_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-held-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>DMX pleaded guilty to charges of drug possession, theft, and animal cruelty stemming from an August 2007 drug raid as well as the May 2008 arrest, at a hearing on December 30, 2008; he was sentenced to 90 days in jail on January 31, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On May 22, 2009, DMX entered a plea agreement/change of plea and pleaded guilty to attempted aggravated assault in jail.</li>
<li>After serving four out of six months for violating drug probation, DMX was released from jail on July 6, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> That day, a television pilot was filmed to portray his road to recovery; however, DMX was arrested three weeks later and the pilot did not evolve into a series.</li>
<li>On July 27, 2010, DMX turned himself in to Los Angeles Metropolitan Court for a reckless driving charge he received in 2002. He was sentenced to serve ninety days in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On November 19, 2010, DMX was arrested in Maricopa County, Arizona on charges of violating probation for a February 24, 2009 aggravated assault on an officer while he was incarcerated. On December 20, 2010, DMX was moved to the Mental Health Unit of the Arizona Alhambra State Prison,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and released on July 18, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On August 24, 2011, DMX was arrested for the tenth time in Maricopa County, this time for speeding, recorded at 102 miles per hour (164&#160;km/h) in a 65-mile-per-hour (105&#160;km/h) zone, reckless driving, and driving with a suspended license. While DMX admitted to speeding, he claimed he was driving 85 miles per hour (137&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_South_Carolina">2013 South Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2013 South Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>On February 13, 2013, DMX was arrested in Spartanburg, South Carolina for driving without a driver's license.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On July 26, 2013, DMX was arrested again in Greenville County, South Carolina and charged with driving under the influence of alcohol as well as driving without a license.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On August 20, 2013, DMX was arrested again in Greer, South Carolina during a traffic stop after a car he was a passenger in made an improper u-turn. He was arrested due to an outstanding warrant for driving under suspension. Four packages of marijuana were also found in the vehicle, and he along with the driver were cited for them.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On November 4, 2013, DMX was again arrested by the Greenville-Spartanburg International Airport police near Greer, South Carolina after police, who were familiar with his prior arrests, noticed DMX behind the wheel of a vehicle at the terminal. DMX was booked on charges of driving with a suspended license, having an uninsured vehicle, and driving an unlicensed vehicle. He was subsequently released after spending three hours in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_New_York">2015 New York</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2015 New York">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>On April 5, 2015, a man accused DMX of robbing him.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On June 26, 2015, DMX was arrested in New York, charged with robbery in Newark, New Jersey and failure to pay child support.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On July 14, 2015, DMX was sentenced to six months in jail for failure to pay $400,000 in child support.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On December 14, 2015, an arrest warrant was issued for DMX after he missed a court hearing to address child support issues with his ex-wife Tashera Simmons and their four children.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.932019:_Tax_fraud_conviction"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–2019:_Tax_fraud_conviction">2017–2019: Tax fraud conviction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2017–2019: Tax fraud conviction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2017, DMX was charged with 14 federal counts of tax fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Federal prosecutors charged him with failing to file <a href="/wiki/Income_tax_returns" class="mw-redirect" title="Income tax returns">income tax returns</a> from 2010 to 2015 (a period when he earned at least $2.3&#160;million). DMX pleaded guilty to a single count of tax fraud in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Moynihan_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moynihan-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> DMX was originally free pending sentencing but was remanded to jail in January 2018 after leaving a drug treatment program ordered by the court and relapsing with cocaine and oxycodone.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018, Judge <a href="/wiki/Jed_S._Rakoff" title="Jed S. Rakoff">Jed S. Rakoff</a> sentenced DMX to one year in prison followed by three years of supervised release. The court also ordered DMX to pay $2.29&#160;million in restitution to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Moynihan_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moynihan-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> He was released from prison on January 25, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_problems_and_death">Health problems and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health problems and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Simmons claimed he became addicted to crack cocaine when he was 14 years old, after Ready Ron tricked him into smoking a marijuana cigarette laced with the drug.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-curse_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curse-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Simmons entered <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">drug rehabilitation</a> several times including in 2002, 2017, and 2019, when he cancelled concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 10, 2016, Simmons was found unresponsive in a parking lot at a Ramada Inn in Yonkers, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-lifeless_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifeless-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> He was resuscitated by first responders and intravenously given <a href="/wiki/Naloxone" title="Naloxone">Narcan</a>, an opioid-reversal drug; he responded quickly to Narcan and became semi-conscious.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Simmons was subsequently rushed to the hospital. A witness said he ingested some type of substance before collapsing, but police found no illegal substances on the property.<sup id="cite_ref-lifeless_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifeless-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Simmons stated that it was from an asthma attack.<sup id="cite_ref-lifeless_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifeless-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains,_New_York.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg/220px-DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg/330px-DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg/440px-DMX_Shrine_in_White_Plains%2C_New_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption>DMX shrine outside White Plains Hospital, where he died</figcaption></figure>
<p>On April 2, 2021, at approximately 11:00 pm,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Simmons was rushed to White Plains Hospital, where he was reported to be in critical condition following a heart attack at his home possibly resulting from a drug overdose.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The next day, his attorney Murray Richman confirmed Simmons was on life support.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> That same night, Simmons suffered <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hypoxia" title="Cerebral hypoxia">cerebral hypoxia</a> as paramedics attempted to resuscitate him for 30 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Simmons's former manager, Nakia Walker, said he was in a "vegetative state" with "lung and brain failure and no current brain activity".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> His manager, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rifkind" title="Steve Rifkind">Steve Rifkind</a>, stated Simmons was <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">comatose</a> and that he was set to undergo tests to determine his brain's functionality and his family will "determine what's best from there".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the morning of April 9, 2021, Simmons lost functionality in multiple essential organs, reportedly his liver, kidneys, and lungs,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and was pronounced dead shortly after, at age 50. It was revealed on July 8 by the Westchester County Medical Examiner's Office that Simmons' official cause of death was a cocaine-induced heart attack.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
