<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style=";">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>"Throughout his nearly three-decade career, DMX came to embody passion, rawness, and pure emotional honesty like few hip-hop artists ever have, barking his way through hits like "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Get_at_Me_Dog" title="Get at Me Dog">Get at Me Dog</a>" one moment, and repenting and philosophizing on tracks like "<a href="/wiki/Slippin%27" title="Slippin&#39;">Slippin</a>'" the next. His was a decidedly anti-commercial approach, but it worked, and it made him the genre's first new superstar in the wake of the killings of <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">the Notorious B.I.G.</a> To this day, few have been able to reach the heights he did—he's the only rapper to have his first five studio albums debut at no. 1, and he was the first living hip-hop artist to have two projects go <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> in the same year."<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/The_Ringer_(website)" title="The Ringer (website)">The Ringer</a> wrote upon DMX's death</cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Various celebrities paid tribute through outlets like social media including former NFL player <a href="/wiki/Torrey_Smith" title="Torrey Smith">Torrey Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/LeBron_James" title="LeBron James">LeBron James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O&#39;Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Union" title="Gabrielle Union">Gabrielle Union</a> (who co-starred with DMX in the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/Cradle_2_the_Grave" title="Cradle 2 the Grave">Cradle 2 the Grave</a></i>, along with <a href="/wiki/Jet_Li" title="Jet Li">Jet Li</a> (who also paid tribute)), Backstreet Boys member <a href="/wiki/AJ_McLean" title="AJ McLean">AJ McLean</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a> (who DMX collaborated with including on the hit single, "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>"),<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eve_(rapper)" title="Eve (rapper)">Eve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A "Celebration of Life" took place on April 24, 2021, led by <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Service_Choir" title="Sunday Service Choir">Sunday Service Choir</a>. They performed several songs in honor of DMX. The memorial took place at <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a> in Brooklyn with a limited capacity of 1,900. It was livestreamed on DMX's YouTube and Instagram accounts. On the way to Barclays, DMX's casket was carried by a black monster truck with "Long live DMX" painted on the side. A procession of hundreds of motorcyclists, in homage to the hip-hop collective Ruff Ryders, rode from DMX's birthplace of Yonkers, New York to Barclays Center. In between performances, people gave speeches including Eve, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, Swizz Beatz and <a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders_Entertainment" title="Ruff Ryders Entertainment">Ruff Ryders</a> founders Joaquin "Waah" Dean &amp; Darin "Dee" Dean. Kanye West was also confirmed to be in attendance of the celebration, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DMX's funeral ("DMX's Homegoing Celebration") took place in Brooklyn at the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Cultural_Center" title="Christian Cultural Center">Christian Cultural Center</a> on April 25, 2021. It was livestreamed on the <a href="/wiki/BET_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="BET Network">BET Network</a> and its YouTube channel. It lasted around five hours to a limited capacity of 2,000 people. DMX's casket was in the color red and featured the word "FAITH" in large printing. It was featured in the front of the room. People who were in attendance included Nas, <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> and Swizz Beatz as well as the pastor of the church, Reverend A.R. Bernard. <a href="/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan" title="Louis Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>, a leader of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a>, joined the service via Zoom. With the exception of Alicia Keys, Nas and Lil Kim, they all gave speeches. DMX's former wife, Tashera Simmons and Ruff Ryders founders Waah &amp; Dee also gave a speech. There was some controversial testimonies like former <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Lyor_Cohen" title="Lyor Cohen">Lyor Cohen</a>, when his video featured an overhead view of a beach and explained how Earl Simmons was a wonderful man while DMX was a gremlin. Additionally, Def Jam cofounder <a href="/wiki/Russell_Simmons" title="Russell Simmons">Russell Simmons</a> compared his own issues with drug abuse to DMX via video. The homegoing ended with DMX's obituary read on stage and a virtual performance from <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the funeral, New York City community leader and peacemaker Erica Ford presented DMX's family several citations and proclamations from the New York governor's and Senate's office, including a proclamation from the New York state Senate declaring December 18—DMX's birthday—"Earl 'DMX' Simmons Day." Additional citations came from Gov. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> and Mayor <a href="/wiki/Mike_Spano" title="Mike Spano">Mike Spano</a> of Yonkers (the hometown of DMX). Cuomo had the flag flying over the state <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Capitol" title="New York State Capitol">capitol</a> on the day of DMX's death presented to his family.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DMX had a significant impact on hip hop music and is considered a "legend" in the genre.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> He's credited for having "defined 2000s rap"<sup id="cite_ref-:bey_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:bey-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and for being "among the most prolific rappers of his era".<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> He broke and set numerous records.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> His early work was vastly different from most mainstream hip hop music at the time; while <a href="/wiki/Puff_Daddy" class="mw-redirect" title="Puff Daddy">Puff Daddy</a> and other artists of the <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a> label were at the height of popularity, characterized by their "big-budget videos, lavish party-throwing, and dancefloor-ready music", DMX achieved success with a more dark, aggressive, "rugged",<sup id="cite_ref-:1_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> less "marketable" style.
</p><p>According to an Apple Music radio host: "It was a complete 180...Puff was controlling the clubs; you were watching Bad Boy Records pop bottles, wear <a href="/wiki/Rolex" title="Rolex">Rolexes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesus_piece_(jewelry)" title="Jesus piece (jewelry)">Jesus pieces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coogi" title="Coogi">Coogi sweaters</a>. Then here comes this crazy energetic figure from Yonkers with the <a href="/wiki/Timbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Timbs">Timbs</a> and the bandanas, running around with pitbulls, giving a perspective on the streets that a lot of people weren't familiar with and taking command of what hip-hop didn't look like." DMX's commercially successful violent lyricism helped popularize the <a href="/wiki/Horrorcore" title="Horrorcore">horrorcore</a> genre.<sup id="cite_ref-:hard_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:hard-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DMX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/DMX_discography" title="DMX discography">DMX discography</a></div>
